## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate as a function of current population size and time, a core problem in population ecology. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent models like logistic growth and extensions with Allee effects or time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible density dependence)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Richards growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (logistic growth with periodic environmental forcing)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Harvesting/immigration logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (logistic with constant immigration or harvesting)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simplest polynomial density dependence)
- Cubic population model: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects including Allee)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (rational density dependence with mortality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP/dt is proportional to P at low densities but bends downward at high P â†’ logistic-type quadratic term P*(1-cP) or rational form P/(1+cP)
- If dP/dt is negative at both very small and very large P â†’ Allee effect structure with cubic terms P*(P-c1)*(1-c2*P)
- If dP/dt shows periodic modulation over time â†’ multiplicative sinusoidal factor (1 + c*sin(Ï‰t)) on the growth term
- If dP/dt vs P curve passes through origin with single hump â†’ classic logistic: growth rate vanishes at P=0 and P=K
- If dP/dt vs P is concave throughout â†’ Gompertz-type logarithmic correction P*log(K/P) rather than polynomial
- If the relationship between dP/dt/P and P is nonlinear â†’ theta-logistic or power-law density dependence P**Î¸
- If dP/dt has a nonzero intercept when Pâ†’0 â†’ immigration/source term present, add constant c to growth equation
- If growth rate per capita (dP/dt)/P changes with time independently of P â†’ non-autonomous model with explicit t-dependent coefficients
